###begin article-title 0
###xml 78 83 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
The Phosphate Transporter PiT1 (Slc20a1) Revealed As a New Essential Gene for Mouse Liver Development
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: LB SBC LC GF. Performed the experiments: LB CL SBC AF CS NP AB MO LC. Analyzed the data: LB CL SBC AF CS NP PUT DP MO LC GF. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: SBC. Wrote the paper: LB.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Background
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 9 16 9 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SLC20a1</italic>
###xml 102 103 102 103 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 344 352 344 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 416 423 416 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
PiT1 (or SLC20a1) encodes a widely expressed plasma membrane protein functioning as a high-affinity Na+-phosphate (Pi) cotransporter. As such, PiT1 is often considered as a ubiquitous supplier of Pi for cellular needs regardless of the lack of experimental data. Although the importance of PiT1 in mineralizing processes have been demonstrated in vitro in osteoblasts, chondrocytes and vascular smooth muscle cells, in vivo evidence is missing.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Methodology/Principal Findings
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 17 24 17 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 150 154 150 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 248 252 248 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 294 298 294 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 752 756 752 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 783 787 783 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 95 99 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1080 1084 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1099 1104 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To determine the in vivo function of PiT1, we generated an allelic series of PiT1 mutations in mice by combination of wild-type, hypomorphic and null PiT1 alleles expressing from 100% to 0% of PiT1. In this report we show that complete deletion of PiT1 results in embryonic lethality at E12.5. PiT1-deficient embryos display severely hypoplastic fetal livers and subsequent reduced hematopoiesis resulting in embryonic death from anemia. We show that the anemia is not due to placental, yolk sac or vascular defects and that hematopoietic progenitors have no cell-autonomous defects in proliferation and differentiation. In contrast, mutant fetal livers display decreased proliferation and massive apoptosis. Animals carrying two copies of hypomorphic PiT1 alleles (resulting in 15% PiT1 expression comparing to wild-type animals) survive at birth but are growth-retarded and anemic. The combination of both hypomorphic and null alleles in heterozygous compounds results in late embryonic lethality (E14.5-E16.5) with phenotypic features intermediate between null and hypomorphic mice. In the three mouse lines generated we could not evidence defects in early skeleton formation.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Conclusion/Significance
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 48 55 48 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 65 69 65 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
This work is the first to illustrate a specific in vivo role for PiT1 by uncovering it as being a critical gene for normal developmental liver growth.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
Introduction
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 155 158 155 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-OHara1">[1]</xref>
###xml 234 235 234 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 229 235 229 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pho-4<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 266 283 266 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neurospora crassa</italic>
###xml 350 351 350 351 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 414 417 414 417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Kavanaugh1">[2]</xref>
###xml 419 422 419 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Olah1">[3]</xref>
###xml 424 427 424 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Miller1">[4]</xref>
###xml 592 595 592 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Saier1">[5]</xref>
###xml 770 773 770 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Miller2">[6]</xref>
###xml 875 878 875 878 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Kavanaugh1">[2]</xref>
###xml 880 883 880 883 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Miller1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1039 1042 1039 1042 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Kavanaugh1">[2]</xref>
###xml 1044 1047 1044 1047 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Uckert1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1049 1052 1049 1052 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Johann1">[8]</xref>
###xml 1223 1226 1223 1226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 1313 1320 1313 1320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 56 61 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 86 90 <span type="species:ncbi:11840">GALV</span>
###xml 92 98 <span type="species:ncbi:9581">Gibbon</span>
###xml 99 102 <span type="species:ncbi:4456">Ape</span>
###xml 266 283 <span type="species:ncbi:5141">Neurospora crassa</span>
###xml 737 743 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
PiT1 is a membrane protein originally identified as the human retrovirus receptor for GALV (Gibbon Ape Leukemia Virus), and was therefore designated GLVR1 [1]. Based on the observation that GLVR1 possesses sequence similarity to pho-4+, a phosphate (Pi) permease of Neurospora crassa, several groups have demonstrated that GLVR1 is a high affinity Na+-dependent Pi transporter, which was consequently renamed PiT1 [2], [3], [4]. PiT1 belongs to the Pi transporter (PiT) family comprising conserved symporters throughout all kingdoms that use either sodium or proton gradients to transport Pi [5]. In mammals, the PiT family is assigned to the solute carrier series SLC20 which also includes PiT2, initially identified as the amphotropic murine retrovirus receptor Ram-1 [6] and subsequently characterized as a Pi transporter with transport characteristics very close to PiT1 [2], [4]. The broad tissue distribution of PiT1 and PiT2 has led to the proposal that these transporters could play a housekeeping role for cellular Pi homeostasis [2], [7], [8]. Although plausible, direct experimental data is lacking. Moreover, significant differences between PiT1 and PiT2 expression levels and ratios are observed among tissues [9], which suggests that these two transporters may have specific and non redundant roles in vivo.
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 136 144 136 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 179 183 179 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 193 197 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 221 222 221 222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 282 286 282 286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck2">[10]</xref>
###xml 300 304 300 304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Suzuki1">[11]</xref>
###xml 343 347 343 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer1">[12]</xref>
###xml 349 353 349 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Zoidis1">[13]</xref>
###xml 392 396 392 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Suzuki2">[14]</xref>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Nielsen1">[15]</xref>
###xml 657 661 657 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Wang1">[16]</xref>
###xml 709 713 703 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer2">[17]</xref>
###xml 945 949 939 943 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Giachelli1">[18]</xref>
###xml 958 966 952 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1057 1061 1051 1055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Li1">[19]</xref>
###xml 1385 1389 1379 1383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Giachelli1">[18]</xref>
###xml 1391 1395 1385 1389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Li1">[19]</xref>
Due to the requirement of large amounts of Pi in bone physiology, the regulation of PiT1 has been well documented in bone and cartilage in vitro models. In osteoblast-like cells, PiT1, but not PiT2, mRNA expression and Na+-Pi cotransport are regulated by various factors such as Pi [10], epinephrine [11], insulin-like growth factor 1 (IGF-1) [12], [13] and bone morphogenic protein 2 (BMP2) [14]. Importantly, PiT1, but not PiT2 is upregulated during osteoblast differentiation, consistent with a dedicated role of PiT1 in this process [15]. Expression and activity of PiT1 in chondrogenic cells was found to be regulated by extracellular Pi concentration [16] and transforming growth factor-beta (TGF-beta) [17]. Moreover, vascular calcification occurring in pathological situations such as hyperphosphatemia-induced calcifications of blood vessels and osteoarthritis, shares a number of similarities with osteogenesis and bone mineralization [18]. Recent in vitro studies have suggested that PiT1 may be implicated in pathological vascular calcification [19]. Particularly, inhibition of Pi uptake by PiT1 small hairpin RNA in cultured vascular smooth muscle cells (VSMCs) blocked the expression of Pi-induced osteogenic differentiation markers, Runx2 and osteopontin, indicating that PiT1 might be a major mechanism for controlling vascular calcification and VSMC phenotypic state [18], [19].
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 84 92 84 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 222 226 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 288 292 288 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer3">[20]</xref>
###xml 339 343 339 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-VillaBellosta1">[21]</xref>
###xml 385 389 385 389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Ravera1">[22]</xref>
###xml 605 611 605 611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">per se</italic>
###xml 637 641 637 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">i.e.</italic>
###xml 888 889 888 889 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1026 1027 1026 1027 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1091 1094 1091 1094 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 1194 1195 1194 1195 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1253 1261 1253 1261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1432 1439 1432 1439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
However, it should be noted that the above-mentioned studies have been conducted in in vitro models and it is not clear which role PiT1 plays in normal bone or vascular physiology. Particularly, the discrete expression of PiT1 in a subset of hypertrophic chondrocytes late in development [20], its weak expression in osteoblasts and VSMCs [21] together with its low transport capacity [22] make it an unlikely candidate to face the tremendous Pi needs for bone or vascular calcification. Moreover, since most studies aimed at elucidating PiT1 regulation and function were conducted in tissues in which Pi per se plays an important role (i.e. mineralized tissues), very little information is available for other tissues. Since PiT1 is expressed in numerous non-mineralizing tissues, it is entirely possible that PiT1 possesses regulated tissue-specific roles going beyond a housekeeping Na+-Pi transport function. In line with this hypothesis, we have recently identified a new function for PiT1, which is independent of its Na+-Pi cotransport activity and is critical for cell proliferation [9]. These recent data show for the first time that PiT1, in addition to its retrovirus receptor and Na+-Pi cotransporter functions, modulates cell proliferation in vitro. The physiological relevance of this third function is unknown, and further illustrates the need for a wider and more physiological approach to decipher the role of PiT1 in vivo.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 101 105 101 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 59 63 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 193 197 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 214 219 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 447 452 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To provide insights into the physiological role of PiT1 in mice, we established an allelic series of PiT1 mutations arising from the combination of normal, hypomorphic and null PiT1 alleles in mice. The new mutant mouse lines described here were used to address the following questions: i) is PiT1 essential for embryo development? ii) are PiT1 and PiT2 physiological roles redundant? iii) is PiT1 essential to skeletal or vessel formation during mouse development? iv) are the growth, development or function of specific organs impaired in the absence of PiT1? In what follows, we provide answers to these questions and report as a key finding that PiT1 deficiency causes mid-gestation embryonic lethality due to an impaired liver development leading to profound anemia.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
Methods
###end title 13
###begin title 14
Animals and Ethics Statement
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 387 388 387 388 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 4 9 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 229 233 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
All mouse models used in the study were on a 129sv/J x C57BL6/J mixed background. Animal care and maintenance were provided through the University Paris Descartes accredited Animal Facility at Necker Faculty of Medicine (Paris). Mice were maintained on rodent laboratory chow (Special Diet Services, Witham, Essex, UK) containing 0.73% calcium, 0.52% phosphate and 600 IU/kg of vitamin D3. All procedures were approved by the Animal Care and Use Committee of the University Paris Descartes.
###end p 15

###xml 40 44 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>

###xml 1236 1245 1232 1241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACTB:FLPe</italic>
###xml 1251 1255 1247 1251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Rodriguez1">[24]</xref>
###xml 1270 1273 1266 1269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</italic>
###xml 1299 1304 1295 1300 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/+</sup>
###xml 1295 1304 1291 1300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1320 1327 1316 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK-Cre</italic>
###xml 1333 1337 1329 1333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Lallemand1">[25]</xref>
###xml 1349 1353 1345 1349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1358 1361 1350 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/+</italic>
###xml 1353 1361 1349 1353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/+</italic></sup>
###xml 1533 1541 1525 1533 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s005">Table S1</xref>
###xml 61 66 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1210 1214 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1246 1250 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1328 1332 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1362 1366 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
A BAC clone (RP23-160G19) containing the genomic sequence of mouse PiT1 was purchased (Invitrogen). Using a recombineering approach [23], we constructed a targeting vector containing PiT1 5'- and 3'-homologous arms (4115 bp and 3645 bp, respectively), a neomycin resistance (neo) cassette flanked by frt sites in intron 5, and a 5' and 3' loxP sites 532 bp upstream and 934 bp downstream from exon 5, respectively. The final vector containing a diphtheria toxin cassette (MC1-DTA) permitting negative selection was verified by sequencing. 129/Sv ES cells were electroporated with 20 microg of linearized targeting vector and selected under G418 treatment. EcoRV digested genomic DNA from 336 ES clones was screened by Southern blotting using a PiT1 5' external probe. Nine positive clones were further analyzed using 5' and 3' probes after digestion of the DNA with two other restriction enzymes, and four clones with the predicted homologous integration were identified. ES cells were injected into C57BL/6 blastocysts, chimaeric males bred to C57BL/6 females and germ-line transmission of the mutation determined by Southern blot analysis and PCR amplification of tail DNA. Heterozygous offspring (PiT1neo/+ mice) were bred either to ACTB:FLPe mice [24] to remove the neo cassette, leading to PiT1lox/+ animals, or to PGK-Cre mice [25] to produce PiT1Delta5/+ mice. Genotyping of neonates and embryos was performed by PCR from tail or yolk sac DNA. Primers used for recombineering, probe amplification and genotyping are listed in Table S1.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
Gene Expression
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 199 203 195 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck3">[26]</xref>
###xml 236 244 232 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s005">Table S1</xref>
###xml 489 493 485 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Livak1">[27]</xref>
###xml 495 502 491 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In situ</italic>
###xml 544 548 540 544 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Moorman1">[28]</xref>
###xml 550 554 546 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 563 571 559 567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s005">Table S1</xref>
Total RNA was isolated from cells and tissue using NucleoSpin RNA columns (Macherey Nagel). Northern analysis of total RNA (25 microg) and RT-PCR amplification were performed as described previously [26]. Specific primers are listed in Table S1. Real-time PCR was performed using SYBR green chemistry (Thermo Scientific) on an ABI Prism 7700 detection system. The glucuronidase or pinin genes were used as reference genes and expression differences were calculated as described previously [27]. In situ hybridization was performed as described [28]. PiT1 probes (Table S1) were transcribed with SP6 or T7 promoters with the DIG RNA labeling kit (Roche Applied Science). Color reaction was performed by using BM purple and sections were counterstained with hematoxilin.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
Hematopoietic Progenitor Cell Assays
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 441 442 431 432 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
Single-cell suspensions from E12.5 fetal livers were plated in 1 ml 1% methylcellulose in Iscove's modified Dulbecco's medium supplemented with 30% FCS, 1% crystallized BSA, and 100 microM 2-mercaptoethanol in the presence of 2 U/ml EPO, 10 ng/ml IL-3, 20 ng/ml thrombopoietin and 100 ng/ml stem cell factor. Samples were plated in duplicate 35-mm bacterial Petri dishes and incubated at 37degreesC in a humidified incubator containing 5% CO2. Colonies were scored at day 2 for CFU-E, day 7 for CFU-granulocyte-macrophage (CFU-GM) and mature burst-forming unit-erythroid (BFU-E), and days 10 to 12 for CFU-granulocyte, erythroid, monocyte, megakaryocyte (CFU-GEMM).
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Immunohistochemistry and Apoptosis Analysis
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 366 370 362 366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Vincent1">[29]</xref>
###xml 776 778 772 774 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 276 279 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 478 482 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Embryos were fixed overnight in 4% buffered formalin. Four-micron sections were produced from paraffin embedded samples and immunohistochemistry was performed according to antibody specification. PECAM-1 (CD-31) was detected in embryos, placental or yolk sac sections using a rat purified anti-CD31 antibody (1/100, clone alpha-MEC 13.3; BD Pharmigen), as described [29]. Proliferating cells were detected with the anti-Ki67 antibody (AbCys). To perform BrDU labeling, pregnant mice were injected intra-peritoneally with 0.3 ml of 50 mg/ml BrDU (Sigma) in PBS. Embryos were harvested after 1 h and fixed overnight in 4% buffered formalin. After embedding in paraffin, detection of BrdU was performed with anti-BrDU antibody (BD Biosciences). To reveal apoptotic cells, DeadEndTM Colorimetric TUNEL System (Promega) and immunohistochemistry using anti-activated caspase 3 (Asp175; Cell Signalling) were used according to the manufacter's instructions.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Partial Hepatectomy
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 36 40 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Eight- to twelve-week-old wild-type mice were subjected to sham operation or two-thirds partial hepatectomy between 9 AM and 12 PM, under general anesthesia with inhaled isoflurane (n = 4 for each genotype and time point). Animals were killed at different times after surgery. Sham animals were operated without any liver resection. Livers were snap frozen into liquid nitrogen for mRNA preparations. All experiments were approved by the institutional committee and were in accordance with European guidelines for the care and use of laboratory animals.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
Embryonic Fibroblasts Culture and Analysis
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 115 116 115 116 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 320 324 320 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Escoubet1">[30]</xref>
###xml 355 356 355 356 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sub>
###xml 387 390 387 390 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
Isolation of MEFs was performed using established procedures and cultured in DMEM supplemented with 10% FBS in 5%CO2 and a humidified atmosphere. For growth curves, 20,000 MEFs were seeded in triplicates in 24-well plates. Every day, cells were trypsinized and counted. Pi transport was measured as previously described [30]. Apparent affinity constant (Km) and maximal transport rate (Vmax) were calculated by nonlinear curve fitting, assuming Michaelis-Menten kinetics.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Immunoblot Analysis
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 139 140 139 140 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 142 143 142 143 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
Cells were lysed for 30 min in ice-cold lysis buffer (150 mM NaCl, 10 mM Tris HCl, 5 mM EDTA, 1% NP40, 0.1% SDS, 0.5% deoxycholate, 1 mM Na3VO4, 1 mM NaF, 5 mM Na pyrophosphate, 0.2 M PMSF and a protease inhibitor cocktail from Roche), and the protein extract was boiled and transferred to PVDF membranes. After blocking with 5% milk/TBST, blots were probed with anti-AMPKsigma, anti-phospho-AMPKsigma (Thr172) antibodies (Cell Signaling Technology) and secondary antibody according to the manufacter's instructions.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
Fatty Acid, Phospholipids and Cholesterol Analysis
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 529 530 525 526 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 1233 1237 1219 1223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Ollero1">[31]</xref>
The lipid-containing organic phase was obtained from erythrocyte suspensions by liquid-liquid extraction with 6 volumes of chloroform/methanol (2:1, v/v), centrifuged at 800 g for 3 min, and the resulting lower phase was aspirated. Cholesterol and phospholipid content were monitored by thin layer chromatography. For cholesterol analysis, aliquots of 4 microl of the different extracts and cholesterol standard were applied to HP-K plates (Whatman, Clifton, NJ), developed in chloroform/acetone (95:5 v/v), stained with the CuSO4 reagent, and developed by charring at 170degreesC. For phospholipid analysis, two sequential mobile phases were utilized as follows: chloroform/triethylamine/ethanol/water (30:30:34:8) and hexane/diethyl ether (100:4.5). The resulting bands were analyzed by the Imagemaster software (Amersham Biosciences). For fatty acid analysis, a 30 microl aliquot of a 1 mg/ml solution of heptadecanoate (17:0, Sigma Chemical, St Louis, MO) in chloroform-methanol (1:1, vol/vol) was added to extracts as an internal standard. Organic extracts were evaporated to dryness under a nitrogen stream and transmethylated with boron trifluoride and methanolic base reagent (BF3-methanol) (Supelco) as previously described [31]. Briefly, dry extracts were resuspended in 0.5 ml of methanolic base, vortexed, and incubated at 100degreesC for 3 min, followed by addition of 14% BF3 in methanol (0.5 ml), vortexing, incubation at 100degreesC for 1 min, addition of hexane (0.5 ml), vortexing, incubation at 100degreesC for 1 min, and addition of 6.5 ml of saturated NaCl. Samples were vortexed and centrifuged at 800 g for 2 min. The hexane upper layer was transferred to a fresh glass tube. Methyl esters of fatty acids were injected into a Hewlett-Packard 5890A gas chromatograph with a flame ionization detector. A 30 m Supelcowax column (Supelco) (0.5 mm internal diameter) was used. The oven temperature was 150degreesC for 2 min, increased to 200degreesC for 5 min, held at 200degreesC for 4 min, increased to 240degreesC for 8 min, and after 3 min increased to 260degreesC and held at this temperature until the end of the program. The detector temperature was 300degreesC. Fatty acid methyl ester peaks were identified by comparison of retention times with a standard mixture of fatty acid methyl esters (Supelco) and quantified by comparison with the internal standard detector response.
###end p 31
###begin title 32
Cartilage and Bone Staining
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 175 179 175 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-McLeod1">[32]</xref>
###xml 62 66 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
For staining and visualization of whole skeletons, fetuses or mice were dissected and stained with alizarin red S or alcian blue 8GX (Sigma), or both, as described previously [32].
###end p 33
###begin title 34
Results
###end title 34
###begin title 35
###xml 16 20 16 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
Generation of a PiT1 Mutant Allelic Series
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 17 24 17 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 229 233 229 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">loxP</italic>
###xml 253 257 253 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 292 295 292 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</italic>
###xml 317 320 317 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">frt</italic>
###xml 340 347 340 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1A</xref>
###xml 468 472 468 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 569 582 569 582 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1B and C</xref>
###xml 622 627 622 627 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>
###xml 618 627 618 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/+</sup></italic>
###xml 656 663 656 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1D</xref>
###xml 601 605 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 641 645 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To determine the in vivo function of PiT1, we targeted the PiT1 locus by homologous recombination in ES cells and generated an allelic series of mutations ranging from mild impairment to elimination of PiT1 function. We inserted loxP sites 5' and 3' to PiT1 exon 5 and a neomycin resistance (neo) cassette flanked by frt sites in intron 5 (Fig. 1A). Cre-mediated deletion of exon 5 is expected to produce a frame shift of the remaining sequence and convert the floxed PiT1 allele to a null allele. Correctly targeted ES cells were identified by Southern blot analysis (Fig. 1B and C), chimeric mutant mice derived and PiT1neo/+ heterozygous mice obtained (Fig. 1D).
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
Generation of an allelic series of mutations at the PiT1 locus.
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 1 2 1 2 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>

###xml 1210 1211 1206 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>

###xml 1542 1546 1538 1542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1645 1646 1641 1642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1656 1657 1652 1653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 258 262 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 891 895 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1020 1024 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1085 1089 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) Schematic representation of PiT1 alleles and targeting vector representing intronic DNA (horizontal lines), PiT1 exons (black boxes) a neo cassette flanked by frt sites (unfilled box) and a diphtheria toxin cassette (hatched box). Heterozygous PiT1neo/+ mice were produced as described. Flp-mediated recombination at frt sites generates the PiT1lox allele, whereas Cre-mediated recombination at loxP sites (open triangles) generates the PiT1Delta5 allele. The positions of restriction sites used for Southern blot screening are shown: E, EcoRV; N, NheI; A, ApaLI. (B) Southern blot analysis of EcoRV-digested DNA from G418-resistant ES cell clones. The wild-type fragment is 33 kb in size, whereas correct recombination generates a 15.4 kb fragment using a 5' probe and a 17.3 kb fragment using a 3' probe (bar). A correctly targeted clone is represented (#18). (C) Genotype analysis of mice heterozygous for the various PiT1 alleles. Southern blots were performed on ApaLI or NheI-digested kidney DNA isolated from mice as indicated, using 5' and 3' probes. (D) PCR genotyping of mice from tail genomic DNA. Primer positions (triangles) are indicated in (A) and their sequences are reported in Table S1. (E) Northern blot of E12.5 whole embryo total RNA as indicated, probed with 32P-labeled PiT1 coding region cDNA. (F) Real-time RT-PCR analysis of the expression of the wild-type PiT1 and PiT2 alleles in E11.5 embryos from the PiT1 allelic mutant series, as indicated. Note that PiT2 is overexpressed in situation when the expression PiT1 becomes very low. * and # indicate significant differences as compared to wild-type controls with P<0.05 and P<0.001, respectively (Student's t test).
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 4 11 4 11 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 0 11 0 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 36 41 36 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>

###xml 138 141 138 141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</sup>

###xml 381 384 381 384 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</sup>

###xml 617 622 617 622 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>

###xml 698 705 698 705 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1F</xref>

###xml 820 824 820 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 906 913 906 913 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 902 913 902 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 920 928 920 928 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s006">Table S2</xref>
###xml 945 948 945 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo</italic>
###xml 962 967 962 967 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>
###xml 958 967 958 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1007 1011 1007 1011 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Rodriguez1">[24]</xref>
###xml 1028 1033 1028 1033 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/+</sup>
###xml 1024 1033 1024 1033 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1112 1117 1112 1117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/+</sup>
###xml 1108 1117 1108 1117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1217 1220 1217 1220 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox</sup>
###xml 1213 1220 1213 1220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox</sup></italic>
###xml 1316 1320 1316 1320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1355 1360 1355 1360 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/+</sup>
###xml 1351 1360 1351 1360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1369 1376 1369 1376 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/lox</sup>
###xml 1365 1376 1365 1376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/lox</sup></italic>
###xml 1383 1390 1383 1390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1F</xref>
###xml 12 16 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1002 1006 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1377 1381 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
PiT1neo/neo mice resulting from PiT1neo/+ intercrosses were born at a lower than expected Mendelian frequency (Table S2). Analysis of PiT1neo transcripts demonstrated an aberrant splicing due to the presence of cryptic splice sites resulting in a hybrid mRNA containing an additional portion of PiT1 intron 5 and the coding sequence of neo (Fig. S1A and B). Translation of the PiT1neo transcript would produce a non-functional PiT1 protein lacking exons 6 to 11 due to the presence of an in frame stop codon 65 bases downstream to exon 5. Accordingly, wild-type PiT1 mRNA levels are significantly reduced both in PiT1neo/+ and PiT1neo/neo E11.5 embryo (35% and 15% of the wild-type, respectively) (Fig. 1F). These results indicate that PiT1neo is a hypomorphic allele, leading to a reduction in the amount of functional PiT1 gene expression, most probably accounting for the non-Mendelian frequency of PiT1neo/neo pups (Table S2). To excise the neo cassette PiT1neo/+ animals were crossed to ACTB:FLPe mice [24], leading to PiT1lox/+ offspring. A Mendelian distribution was observed in progeny obtained from PiT1lox/+ intercrosses and no phenotypic difference was observed among genotypes, demonstrating that the PiT1lox allele is functionally equivalent to the wild-type allele. Accordingly, the level of wild-type PiT1 mRNA was found normal in both PiT1lox/+ and PiT1lox/lox mice (Fig. 1F).
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 12 16 12 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 35 40 35 40 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>
###xml 31 40 31 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/+</sup></italic>
###xml 68 75 68 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PGK-Cre</italic>
###xml 96 100 96 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Lallemand1">[25]</xref>
###xml 179 191 179 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1C to E</xref>
###xml 194 198 194 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 203 206 199 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/+</italic>
###xml 198 206 198 202 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/+</italic></sup>
###xml 248 251 244 247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 244 251 240 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 373 380 369 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0009148-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 395 399 391 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 404 406 396 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 411 412 399 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 399 412 395 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 505 509 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 553 560 541 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0009148-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 41 45 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 91 95 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 207 211 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To generate PiT1-null animals, PiT1neo/+ mice were crossed with the PGK-Cre deleter strain mice [25]. The deletion was confirmed by Southern blot, PCR and northern blot analysis (Fig. 1C to E). PiT1Delta5/+ mice appeared indistinguishable from PiT1+/+ littermates, were viable and fertile producing offspring in normal Mendelian ratios when crossed with wild-type animals (Table 1). However, no PiT1Delta5/Delta5 offspring were found among 208 newborn pups from heterozygote intercrosses, indicating that PiT1 disruption results in embryonic lethality (Table 1).
###end p 40

###xml 401 414 377 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 504 508 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 539 546 507 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1F</xref>
###xml 306 310 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 422 426 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 490 494 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Similarly, PiT1neo/Delta5 compound heterozygotes resulting from PiT1neo/+ and PiT1Delta5/+ matings were not viable (Table S3). Wild-type PiT1 mRNA levels in E12.5 PiT1neo/Delta5 embryos represented 6% of normal levels whereas PiT2 expression was increased, as was seen in PiT1neo/neo and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 mice (Fig. 1F). Hence, together with the PiT1+/+, PiT1neo/+, PiT1Delta5/+, PiT1neo/neo and PiT1Delta5/Delta5, these mice contribute to the establishment of an allelic series of mutant mice in which PiT1 is expressed from 100% to 0% (Fig. 1F).
###end p 45
###begin title 46
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 77 82 77 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</italic>
###xml 82 84 78 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 84 89 80 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</italic>
###xml 89 90 81 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 77 90 77 82 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5/</italic><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5</italic></sup>
Mid-Gestation Lethality Due to Defective Liver Development and Anemia in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 Embryos
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 41 45 41 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 156 163 156 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0009148-t001">Table 1</xref>

###xml 370 374 354 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 379 381 359 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 386 387 362 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 374 387 358 363 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 545 552 521 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2A</xref>
###xml 565 569 541 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 574 576 546 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>

###xml 808 821 776 789 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2C and D</xref>
###xml 986 993 954 961 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2E</xref>
###xml 1085 1092 1053 1060 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2F</xref>
###xml 1153 1156 1121 1124 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1149 1156 1117 1124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1161 1165 1129 1133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1170 1172 1134 1136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1177 1178 1137 1138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1165 1178 1133 1138 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1367 1374 1323 1330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2G</xref>
###xml 1402 1406 1358 1362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1411 1413 1363 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1418 1419 1366 1367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1406 1419 1362 1367 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1548 1552 1496 1500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1557 1559 1501 1503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1564 1565 1504 1505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1552 1565 1500 1505 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1603 1616 1543 1556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2H and I</xref>
###xml 1717 1730 1657 1670 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g002">Fig. 2J and K</xref>
To identify at which developmental stage PiT1-null embryos die, genotyping of litters harvested from serial timed matings from E3.5 to birth was performed (Table 1). Results revealed that living PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos were detected up to E12.5, and that no PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos survived after this stage. Until E9.5 no macroscopic abnormalities were observed in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos by gross anatomical and histological examinations. At E10.5, embryos were found to be slightly growth retarded, without morphological abnormalities (Fig. 2A). At E12.5, PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos could be easily recognized by their significant growth retardation and profound anemia (Fig. 2B). The most striking defect was observed in the developing liver, occupying only a small fraction of the abdominal areas (Fig. 2C and D). Morphological examination showed that E12.5 mutant livers, composed of four lobes, were extremely pale and severely reduced in size as compared to normal livers (Fig. 2E). Total liver nucleated cell counts represented only 2% of wild-type livers at this stage (Fig. 2F). Real-time RT-PCR analysis of RNA extracted from E12.5 PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos demonstrated that the level of albumin and alpha-fetoprotein transcripts in mutant embryos was markedly reduced, further suggesting the decrease in hepatoblast number or function (Fig. 2G). Histological analysis of PiT1Delta5/Delta5 E12.5 livers further confirmed the reduced cellularity and increased empty space, indicating less dense packing of cells in the PiT1Delta5/Delta5 as compared to the wild-type livers (Fig. 2H and I). Hypocellularity and presence of large sinuses in the mutant livers were already visible at E11.5 (Fig. 2J and K).
###end p 47
###begin title 48
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
Disruption of the PiT1 gene leads to defective liver development and anemia.

###xml 59 72 59 64 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5/</italic><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5</italic></sup>
Absence of Placental, Yolk Sac and Vascular Defects in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 Embryos
###end title 50
###begin p 51
###xml 123 127 123 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 132 134 128 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 139 140 131 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 127 140 127 132 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 240 248 232 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s002">Fig. S2A</xref>
###xml 329 333 321 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 338 340 326 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 345 346 329 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 333 346 325 330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 437 445 421 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s002">Fig. S2B</xref>
###xml 588 596 572 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s002">Fig. S2F</xref>
We next evaluated whether defects in placenta, yolk sac or vasculature could be responsible of the observed anemia seen in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos. Wild-type and mutant placentas appeared similar, except that mutant placentas were paler (Fig. S2A). The chorionic plate and labyrinthine trophoblast layer were well developed in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 placentas, and no differences in vascularization were evidenced on histological sections (Fig. S2B to E). In addition, we did not detect differences in placental cell proliferation and apoptotic signals between mutant and control placentas (Fig. S2F to I). This suggests that the observed anemia is highly unlikely to be caused by defects in placental development and subsequent failure to establish the maternal-fetal interface for oxygen and nutrient exchange.
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 214 227 214 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g003">Fig. 3A and B</xref>
###xml 436 448 436 448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g003">Fig. 3C to E</xref>
###xml 525 529 525 529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 534 536 530 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 541 542 533 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 529 542 529 534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 626 630 618 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 635 637 623 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 642 643 626 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 630 643 622 627 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 653 665 637 649 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g003">Fig. 3F to I</xref>
###xml 1006 1019 990 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g003">Fig. 3J and K</xref>
No hemorrhage was found in the mutant embryos, suggesting that a default in the vasculature is unlikely to be responsible for the anemia. At E11.5 the tree-like architecture of the vasculature was clearly visible (Fig. 3A and B), although severe decrease in red blood cells number impedes from visualizing the entire network. Close examination of E12.5 mutant yolk sac revealed a highly developed vasculature devoid of red blood cells (Fig. 3C to E). Histological examination and anti-PECAM-1 staining of endothelial cell of PiT1Delta5/Delta5 yolk sac sections confirmed that major defects in the vasculature were absent from PiT1Delta5/Delta5 mutants (Fig. 3F to I). Similarly, no difference in endothelial cell staining could be seen between wild-type and mutant sections throughout the entire embryo (data not shown). Anti-PECAM-1 staining on liver serial sections showed that although vessels appeared more numerous on the mutant livers, this was largely due to the severely reduced size of the liver (Fig. 3J and K). While these data do not exclude the possible existence of minor defects, they indicate that there were no major vascular defects shortly before the occurrence of embryonic death at E12.5.
###end p 52

###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 4 9 4 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</italic>

###xml 977 981 920 924 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Trimborn1">[34]</xref>

###xml 1356 1360 1291 1295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1547 1551 1482 1486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Isern1">[35]</xref>
###xml 273 277 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 775 780 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Peripheral blood smears showed that the majority of erythroid cells in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 mutants were larger than in the wild-type (Fig. 4A and B), which was confirmed by measuring the cell and nucleus mean diameters of erythroid cells in the PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 mice (Fig. 4C). Since primitive erythroid precursors are approximately twice as large and contain twice as much hemoglobin than their mature counterparts [33], this suggests that PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos have a higher proportion of immature erythroid cells. We confirmed this by quantifying the expression of hemoglobin genes (Fig. 4D). Hemoglobin molecules contain globin chains derived both from the alpha-globin (Hbb-a) and beta-globin (Hbb-b) gene loci. Although definitive erythroid cells in the mouse express alpha1-globin, alpha2-globin, beta1-globin, and beta2-globin, primitive erythroid cells in addition express zeta-globin (Hba-x), betaH1-globin (Hbb-bh1), and epsilony-globin (Hbb-y) [33], [34]. We found that the amount of adult and fetal forms of globin chains in the mutant represented 2 to 9% and 19 to 25% of the wild-type, respectively. Accordingly, the ratios between fetal and adult forms of hemoglobin was higher in E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 livers than in the wild-type (Fig. 4D), suggesting that the maturational globin switching may be impaired or delayed in PiT1-deficient embryos. Alternatively, a defect in the developmental niche provided by the fetal liver for the maturation and enucleation of primitive erythrocytes may explain this phenotype [35].
###end p 56

###xml 127 131 127 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 422 435 414 419 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 552 564 536 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g004">Fig. 4E to H</xref>
###xml 632 633 616 617 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>

###xml 786 787 762 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 774 787 758 763 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 863 875 839 851 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g004">Fig. 4E to H</xref>
###xml 927 930 903 906 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>

###xml 939 952 915 920 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1208 1211 1172 1175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1204 1211 1168 1175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1216 1220 1180 1184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1225 1227 1185 1187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1232 1233 1188 1189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1220 1233 1184 1189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1286 1290 1242 1246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1295 1297 1247 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1302 1303 1250 1251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1290 1303 1246 1251 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1471 1475 1419 1423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1480 1482 1424 1426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1487 1488 1427 1428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1475 1488 1423 1428 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1594 1602 1534 1542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1648 1652 1588 1592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1657 1659 1593 1595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1664 1665 1596 1597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1652 1665 1592 1597 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
We conducted in vitro progenitor assays to characterize whether the erythropoietic defect in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos could result from either an intrinsic defect in hematopoietic progenitors or a failure in the ability of the fetal-liver microenvironment to support erythropoiesis. Single cell suspensions cultured in methylcellulose showed that the absolute number of CFU-E, BFU-E, CFU-GM and CFU-GEMM colonies per PiT1Delta5/Delta5 fetal liver were reduced 48-, 90-, 74- and 46-fold, respectively, as compared with values in wild-type littermates (Fig. 4E to H). However, when results were expressed as number of colonies per 105 nucleated fetal-liver cells, no significant difference was found between normal and mutant livers suggesting that a similar fraction of PiT1Delta5/Delta5 and wild-type fetal livers are composed of hematopoietic cell progenitors (Fig. 4E to H). The ratio of BFU-Es to CFU-Es was similar in PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos, suggesting that there was no defect in the terminal differentiation of erythroid progenitors. Both the size of CFU-E, BFU-E, CFU-GM and CFU-GEMM colonies and the number of cells per colony were similar (836+/-94 and 766+/-58 cells/colony for PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5, respectively). These results suggest that although PiT1Delta5/Delta5 fetal livers were severely hypoplastic, some hematopoietic stem cells do migrate there and have the potential to give rise to all erythropoietic lineages. Because the PiT1Delta5/Delta5 hematopoietic committed progenitor cells were able to proliferate and differentiate normally when tested in vitro, this suggests that the anemia seen in E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos is unlikely to arise from a hematopoietic cell-autonomous defect.
###end p 59
###begin title 60
###xml 47 51 47 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 51 56 51 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</italic>
###xml 56 58 52 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 58 63 54 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</italic>
###xml 63 64 55 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 51 64 51 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5/</italic><italic>&#916;</italic><italic>5</italic></sup>
Increased Apoptosis and Reduced Growth Rate in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 Livers
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 325 338 325 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5A and B</xref>
###xml 407 419 407 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5C to F</xref>
###xml 532 545 532 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5E and F</xref>
###xml 646 650 646 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 662 663 654 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 650 663 650 655 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 728 741 720 733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5G and H</xref>
###xml 837 850 829 842 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5I and J</xref>
###xml 1003 1007 995 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1012 1014 1000 1002 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1019 1020 1003 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1007 1020 999 1004 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1051 1064 1035 1048 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5K and L</xref>
###xml 1335 1339 1319 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1415 1428 1399 1412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g005">Fig. 5M and N</xref>
###xml 1645 1658 1629 1642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g006">Fig. 6A and B</xref>
###xml 1938 1951 1922 1935 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g006">Fig. 6C and D</xref>
###xml 2198 2211 2182 2195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g006">Fig. 6E and F</xref>
We next asked whether the reduction in liver cell density was caused by reduced proliferation or whether a loss of liver cells had occurred due to cell death. Histological sections revealed that most of the E12.5 mutant livers displayed abundant fragmented pyknotic nuclei, whereas only few were visible on control sections (Fig. 5A and B). TUNEL staining of liver sections confirmed the above observation (Fig. 5C to F). Of interest, the level of TUNEL staining in E11.5 mutant livers was comparable to that of wild-type controls (Fig. 5E and F). Immunodetection of activated caspase 3, revealed a significant number of apoptotic cells in E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 livers, while few apoptotic cells were found in control livers (Fig. 5G and H). The level of activated caspase 3 in E11.5 mutant livers was comparable to that of wild-type (Fig. 5I and J). We next examined the proliferation status of PiT1-deficient livers. Staining with the proliferation marker Ki67 was less intense in sections of E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 livers than in the wild-type (Fig. 5K and L). These results were confirmed by performing BrDU pulse-labeling of dividing cells in E11.5 pregnant females, and subsequent detection of BrDU-positive cells. Wild-type fetal livers showed heavy nuclear staining in the entire liver, whereas BrDU staining was reduced in PiT1-null samples directly demonstrating a subnormal growth rate in this organ (Fig. 5M and N). Antibodies recognizing the fetal hepatocyte marker cytokeratin 18 (CK18) revealed label-positive cells in PiT1 mutant embryos at E12.5, suggesting that, at least at this stage, developing hepatocytes were present (Fig. 6A and B). However, it was notable that CK18 staining revealed disorganized tissue architecture and that marker-positive cells were often rounded up or pyknotic. Staining against the erythroid cell marker Ter119 revealed a significant reduction in marker-positive cells in mutant livers (Fig. 6C and D), correlating with the loss of erythroid lineage cells. Activated caspase 3 staining of sections from the same livers revealed that Ter119-positive cells were not labeled in mutant sections whereas apoptosis was evident in CK18-expressing cells (Fig. 6E and F). Thus, while developing hepatocytes emerge in PiT1 mutant livers at E12.5, loss of hepatocytes by apoptosis is a frequent occurrence whereas the scarcity of Ter119-labeled cells in mutant livers is unlikely to correlate with apoptotic activity.
###end p 61

###begin p 67

###xml 500 513 500 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g007">Fig. 7A and B</xref>
###xml 585 589 585 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 749 753 749 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 839 843 839 843 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 977 984 977 984 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g007">Fig. 7C</xref>
###xml 1042 1046 1042 1046 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 1214 1221 1214 1221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g007">Fig. 7D</xref>
###xml 1258 1262 1258 1262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
