###xml 1353 1355 1349 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1360 1361 1352 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1348 1361 1348 1353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1394 1398 1386 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 1449 1456 1441 1448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g007">Fig. 7E</xref>
###xml 1536 1543 1528 1535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g001">Fig. 1F</xref>
###xml 1733 1736 1725 1728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 2043 2047 2035 2039 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Frei1">[36]</xref>
###xml 2114 2118 2106 2110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2331 2335 2323 2327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 2361 2365 2353 2357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2437 2444 2429 2436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g007">Fig. 7F</xref>
###xml 2462 2466 2454 2458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2655 2659 2647 2651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2734 2738 2726 2730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2743 2745 2731 2733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 2750 2751 2734 2735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 2738 2751 2730 2735 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 46 51 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 53 56 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 61 66 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1822 1827 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1903 1908 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 2032 2035 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 2185 2189 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Although widespread, PiT1 expression in adult mouse, rat and human is rather variable between tissues and is low in the adult liver [2], [7], [8]. Our in situ hybridization (ISH) experiments on E12.5 wild-type embryo sections demonstrated that PiT1 was expressed at low levels throughout the embryo, except in the liver. Faint PiT1 expression was detected in the developing brain as previously described [8], but this signal was much lower than the high level of expression found in the fetal liver (Fig. 7A and B). This result is in sharp contrast with the low level of expression of PiT1 in adult livers, but is consistent with a role of PiT1 during developmental liver growth. We confirmed these results by quantifying the expression of PiT1 and PiT2 in fetal E12.5 and post-natal P15 wild-type livers by real-time RT-PCR. The level of PiT1 in the fetal liver was 4.4-fold higher than that in the post-natal liver, whereas fetal and post-natal PiT2 expression were similar (Fig. 7C). Moreover, quantification of the relative expression of PiT1 and PiT2 in wild-type fetal and post-natal livers revealed that PiT1 expression was 3.4-fold higher in fetal livers and 1.7-fold lower in post natal livers than PiT2 (Fig. 7D), further illustrating the need for PiT1 during developmental liver growth. Of importance, while PiT1 was undetectable in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 E12.5 livers, the expression of PiT2 was 1.5-fold higher than in the wild-type livers (Fig. 7E), a value that is comparable to the increase found in the whole mutant embryo (Fig. 1F). To determine in which cell types PiT1 was most expressed, we performed immunostaining of PiT1 on wild-type and mutant sections using PiT1 antibodies from commercial or laboratory sources [9]. Unfortunately, we are unable to generate a specific signal using the available anti-mouse antibodies, and the expression of PiT1 in specific liver cell types during mouse development remains an open question. However, PiT1 has been localized in adult hepatocytes, but not in cholangiocytes, in rat livers [36]. Consistent with this finding, we further illustrated the role of PiT1 in liver growth by performing partial hepatectomy on normal adult mice. In this model, the remnant liver undergoes rapid division to re-establish the original weight of the organ. Our results show that, although PiT2 expression is unchanged, PiT1 is highly (3.5-fold) induced within 2 h following partial hepatectomy (Fig. 7F) indicating that PiT1 is likely to be essential during the early stage of compensatory liver growth. Although further experiments are necessary, this observation could be consistent with a higher expression of PiT1 in developing versus adult fetal livers and the low proliferation rate of PiT1Delta5/Delta5 livers.
###end p 67
###begin title 68
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
PiT1 expression during liver growth.
###end title 68
###begin p 69
###xml 1 2 1 2 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 4 11 4 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In situ</italic>
###xml 72 76 72 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 211 212 211 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 227 231 227 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 273 274 273 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 286 290 286 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 295 299 295 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 424 425 424 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 541 542 541 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>

###xml 853 857 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) In situ hybridization (ISH) of a wild-type E12.5 embryo shows heavy PiT1 signal in the developing liver (black arrow), whereas low signal is detected in the brain (white arrows) and throughout the embryos. (B) ISH with the PiT1 sense probe gives no signal. Bar, 1 mm. (C) Ratios of PiT1 and PiT2 mRNA expression levels between embryonic (E12.5) and post-natal (P15) wild-type livers, as determined by real-time RT-PCR. (D) PiT1/PiT2 expression ratios in embryonic (E12.5) and post-natal (P15) livers, as determined by real-time RT-PCR. (E) Quantification of the expression of PiT1 and PiT2 in normal and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 E12.5 livers by real-time RT-PCR. Note the 1.5-fold overexpression of PiT2 in PiT1-null livers. (F) Gene induction after partial hepatectomy. Total cellular RNA collected in a time course after partial hepatectomy in wild-type mice was analyzed by real time RT-PCR for the expression of PiT1, PiT2 and PCNA as a marker of proliferation. Results are reported after normalization to the expression of Pinin.

###xml 17 21 17 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###begin p 71
###xml 27 31 27 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 145 149 145 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 187 195 187 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 224 226 220 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>

###xml 219 232 219 224 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 382 385 374 377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 378 385 370 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 392 399 384 391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g008">Fig. 8A</xref>
###xml 402 406 394 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 411 414 399 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/+</italic>
###xml 406 414 398 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/+</italic></sup>
###xml 559 560 547 548 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 626 627 614 615 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 651 655 639 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 713 714 701 702 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 728 732 716 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 759 766 747 754 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g008">Fig. 8B</xref>
###xml 857 859 841 843 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 868 871 852 855 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 864 871 848 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 876 880 860 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 885 887 865 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 892 893 868 869 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 880 893 864 869 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 965 968 933 936 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 961 968 929 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 973 977 941 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 982 984 946 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 989 990 949 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 977 990 945 950 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1050 1054 1010 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1069 1073 1029 1033 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1078 1080 1034 1036 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 1085 1086 1037 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1073 1086 1033 1038 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 1161 1165 1113 1117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 1172 1179 1124 1131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g008">Fig. 8C</xref>
###xml 1234 1235 1186 1187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1252 1257 1204 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1-</italic>
###xml 1305 1309 1257 1261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1538 1541 1490 1493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 1563 1570 1515 1522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
As genetic inactivation of PiT1 resulted in embryonic lethality, together with decreased cell proliferation, we evaluated whether the absence of PiT1 could also affect MEFs proliferation in vitro. Results show that PiT1Delta5/Delta5 MEFs proliferated very slowly, displaying a mean doubling time of 38 h, a 2.1-fold increase compared with the doubling time of 18 h observed for PiT1+/+ MEFs (Fig. 8A). PiT1Delta5/+ MEFs had an intermediate growth rate (mean doubling time of 20 h). As the main reported function of PiT1 is to couple inward Pi uptake to the Na+ gradient across the cell plasma membrane, we characterized the Na+-dependent Pi uptake in PiT1-deficient MEFs. Interestingly, our results showed that Na+-Pi uptake in PiT1-null MEFs was unaffected (Fig. 8B), with no change in its kinetic properties (Vmax  = 19.2+/-0.7 and 19.1+/-1.7 nmol.mg prot-1 for PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 MEFs, respectively; Km  = 124.5+/-38.5 and 134.5+/-17.9 microM for PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta5/Delta5 MEFs, respectively). While real-time RT-PCR confirmed that PiT1 expression in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 MEFs was abolished, this was associated with a 1.8-fold overexpression of PiT2 mRNA (Fig. 8C), which could account for the maintenance of normal Na+-Pi transport in PiT1-null MEFs. Maintenance of a normal Pi uptake in PiT1-null MEFs supports the idea that the defect in MEF proliferation was not a consequence of Pi deprivation but resulted in a transport-independent function of PiT1, consistent with our recent data obtained in HepG2 and HeLa cells [9]. However, additional in vivo studies are necessary to assign the observed phenotype to a specific loss of either function of PiT1.
###end p 71
###begin title 72
###xml 14 18 14 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 45 46 45 46 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
Disruption of PiT1 in MEFs does not affect Na+-Pi cotransport but leads to reduced proliferation.
###end title 72

###xml 31 36 31 36 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/+</sup>

###xml 62 73 62 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 176 184 176 184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s006">Table S2</xref>
###xml 223 227 223 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 377 385 377 385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s003">Fig. S3A</xref>
###xml 451 458 449 456 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 447 458 445 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 507 521 503 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s003">Fig. S3A and B</xref>
###xml 630 637 626 633 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 626 637 622 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 925 933 921 929 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s003">Fig. S3B</xref>
###xml 1042 1049 1038 1045 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 1038 1049 1034 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 1089 1092 1085 1088 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1085 1092 1081 1088 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1099 1107 1095 1103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 1396 1403 1392 1399 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 1392 1403 1388 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 1410 1418 1406 1414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 1661 1668 1657 1664 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 1657 1668 1653 1664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 1911 1919 1907 1915 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s003">Fig. S3E</xref>
###xml 2084 2091 2080 2087 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 2080 2091 2076 2087 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 2134 2138 2130 2134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2143 2145 2135 2137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 2150 2151 2138 2139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 2138 2151 2134 2139 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 2351 2359 2339 2347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s009">Table S5</xref>
###xml 2461 2468 2449 2456 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 2457 2468 2445 2456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 2806 2810 2794 2798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Goheen1">[37]</xref>
###xml 2913 2920 2901 2908 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 2909 2920 2897 2908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 3069 3077 3057 3065 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s009">Table S5</xref>
###xml 3216 3222 3204 3210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">per se</italic>
###xml 3258 3265 3246 3253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 3254 3265 3242 3253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 336 340 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 644 648 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 976 980 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1050 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1093 1097 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1236 1240 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1404 1408 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1669 1673 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2092 2096 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2152 2156 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2469 2473 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2921 2925 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3063 3067 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3266 3270 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Genotyping of litters from PiT1neo/+ intercrosses showed that PiT1neo/neo pups were present at a lower frequency than expected (15% vs 25%) reaching only 5% at 2-weeks of age (Table S2), indicating that a low expression of PiT1 is sufficient to bypass the embryonic lethality but results in partial postnatal lethality. The hypomorphic mice that survived were growth retarded (Fig. S3A to C). At birth, the mean weight of pups was 0.9+/-0.1 g for PiT1neo/neo and 1.5+/-0.2 g for wild-type or heterozygotes (Fig. S3A and B). At 2-3 weeks of age, the difference in weight was maximal (2-fold lower than controls). The weight of PiT1neo/neo adult mice ultimately remained approximately 1.3-fold lower than that of controls. The exact origin of the growth retardation is not known, but may be related to the anemia and subsequent hypo-oxygenation of growing tissues, suggested by the pale coloration of newborn hypomorphic pups (Fig. S3B). Peripheral blood analysis of 3-week-old mice showed mild but significant erythrocyte abnormalities in PiT1neo/neo mice as compared to litter-matched PiT1+/+ mice (Table S4). The red blood cell counts, hematocrit, and hemoglobin concentration were significantly lower in hypomorphic than in wild-type mice. The mild anemia seen in the mutant was not explained by decreased formation of erythrocytes, since the reticulocyte number was 2.5-fold higher in the PiT1neo/neo mice (Table S4), consistent with an absence of abnormalities in bone marrow smears (data not shown). Together, these data are rather indicative of hemolytic anemia resulting from peripheral destruction of erythrocytes. Consistent with this possibility, PiT1neo/neo mice displayed a significant splenomegaly, whereas the size of the liver, brain and kidneys were normal (). Similarly, peripheral blood smears showed numerous abnormal red cell morphology, including echinocytes, spherocytes, and schizocytes (Fig. S3E). The origin of the observed phenotype is unknown and can arise either from decreased red cell membrane fluidity or defects in microvascular environment in the PiT1neo/neo mice. The absence of vessel defect in the PiT1Delta5/Delta5 mice argues against the latter hypothesis, although detailed studies must be performed. Analysis of lipid membrane composition of mutant and control red blood cells demonstrated significant changes (Table S5). Monounsaturated fatty acid were increased, whereas polyunsatured fatty acid where decreased in PiT1neo/neo mice as compared to wild-type littermates: mutant red blood cells had higher levels of 16:1n-7 and 18:1n-9 and lower levels of 18:0 fatty acids. However, such changes are not known to be associated with a change in membrane fluidity and may reflect the difference in the lipid membrane composition between erythrocytes and reticulocytes [37]. This latter possibility is further supported by the increase in stearoyl-CoA desaturase index in PiT1neo/neo mice. More importantly, cholesterol concentration and mean cholesterol/phospholipid molar ratio were not different between mutant and control mice (Table S5), arguing against a striking change in erythrocytes membrane fluidity. It remains to be determined, however, whether the decrease of PiT1 per se in the erythrocyte membrane of PiT1neo/neo mice can account for altered erythrocyte membrane morphology.
###end p 75

###xml 837 851 797 811 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s004">Fig. S4F and G</xref>

###xml 974 988 930 944 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s004">Fig. S4H and I</xref>

###xml 1143 1151 1099 1107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0009148.s004">Fig. S4K</xref>
###xml 1239 1243 1195 1199 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/</sup>
###xml 1235 1243 1191 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/</sup></italic>
###xml 1248 1249 1200 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 1243 1249 1199 1201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 41 45 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 145 149 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 270 274 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 314 318 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The compound heterozygous PiT1neo/Delta5 mice express functional PiT1 levels that are intermediate between the PiT1Delta5/Delta5 and PiT1neo/neo mice (Fig. 1F). Accordingly, several phenotypic features were found to lie in severity between the null and hypomorphic PiT1 mice. Embryonic lethality of PiT1neo/Delta5 mice was found to arise later in development than for PiT1Delta5/Delta5 counterparts, occurring between E14.5 and E16.5 (Table S3). At E14.5, PiT1neo/Delta5 embryos were severely anemic (Fig. S4A). At this stage mutant livers were hypoplastic, whereas E12.5 mutants and control livers showed comparable histology (Fig. S4B to E). Consistent with results obtained in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos, no hemorrhage was found in the PiT1neo/Delta5 fetuses and no gross vascular defect could be detected by examination of yolk sacs (Fig. S4F and G). PiT1neo/Delta5 circulating nucleated erythrocytes displayed morphologic features similar to those observed in controls (Fig. S4H and I) but were 6.9-fold more numerous than in controls (Fig. S4J). In addition, the level of embryonic hemoglobin was increased in the compound heterozygotes (Fig. S4K), suggesting that the relative increase in the number of nucleated erythrocytes in PiT1neo/Delta5 is likely to result from the persistence of primitive yolk sac-derived erythrocytes secondary to a liver-defect in definitive erythropoiesis production.
###end p 77
###begin title 78
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 28 32 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Impaired PiT1 Expression in Mice Does Not Affect Early Skeleton Development
###end title 78
###begin p 79
###xml 118 122 118 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 226 230 226 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 235 237 231 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5/</italic>
###xml 242 243 234 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 230 243 230 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 252 255 244 247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 248 255 240 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 265 278 257 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g009">Fig. 9A and B</xref>
###xml 323 327 315 319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/</sup>
###xml 319 327 311 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/</sup></italic>
###xml 332 333 320 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</italic>
###xml 327 333 319 321 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>
###xml 342 345 330 333 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 338 345 326 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 355 367 343 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g009">Fig. 9C to H</xref>
###xml 428 435 416 423 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 424 435 412 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 747 759 735 747 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g009">Fig. 9I to L</xref>
###xml 1054 1061 1042 1049 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 1050 1061 1038 1049 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>
###xml 1070 1073 1058 1061 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 1066 1073 1054 1061 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 1080 1093 1068 1081 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0009148-g009">Fig. 9M and N</xref>
###xml 1123 1130 1111 1118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1140 1144 1128 1132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1217 1221 1205 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 130 134 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1074 1078 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1275 1280 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Since PiT1 has been extensively studied in bone and cartilage, we investigated whether these tissues were affected in PiT1 mutant mice. Alcian blue staining of the initial cartilage matrix revealed no difference between E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 and PiT1+/+ embryos (Fig. 9A and B), or later in development between E15.5 PiT1neo/Delta5 and PiT1+/+ embryos (Fig. 9C to H). Alcian blue/alizarin red S double staining of newborn PiT1neo/neo and wild-type skeletons showed an impaired mineralization of both long bones in which endochondral (arising from cartilaginous mold) ossification takes place, and in the cranial vault and portions of the upper facial skeleton that develop by intramembranous ossification without replacing a cartilaginous mold (Fig. 9I to L). However, these differences were not seen on all of the hypomorphic newborn pups (data not shown), suggesting that the impaired mineralization may have been already corrected. Consistent with this hypothesis, staining of 2-weeks-old skeletons demonstrated no detectable difference between PiT1neo/neo and PiT1+/+ mice (Fig. 9M and N). Our data do not exclude an in vivo role for PiT1 in bone and cartilage biology, but indicate that a normal expression of PiT1 is not essential for early skeleton formation during mouse development.
###end p 79
###begin title 80
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 28 32 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Impaired PiT1 expression in mice does not affect early skeleton development.
###end title 80

###xml 187 188 175 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>

###xml 570 573 558 561 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 566 573 554 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 582 589 570 577 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">neo/neo</sup>
###xml 578 589 566 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>neo/neo</sup></italic>

###begin title 82
Discussion
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 75 79 75 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 124 128 124 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 61 65 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
In this report we have generated an allelic series of mutant mice in which PiT1 is expressed from 100% to 0%. Disruption of PiT1 leads to mid-gestation lethality due to severe defects in liver development, arising from reduced proliferation and massive apoptosis of liver cells. Impaired liver development causes dramatic anemia eventually leading to the death of the embryo. No placental, yolk sac or vascular defects were identified.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 34 38 34 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 320 324 320 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 413 416 413 416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Kavanaugh1">[2]</xref>
###xml 418 421 418 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Uckert1">[7]</xref>
###xml 423 426 423 426 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Johann1">[8]</xref>
###xml 541 545 541 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 653 657 653 657 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer3">[20]</xref>
###xml 778 782 778 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 808 812 808 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 874 878 874 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 882 886 882 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 919 923 919 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 955 959 955 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1041 1045 1041 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1106 1110 1106 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 635 640 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1289 1294 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Considering the available data on PiT1, our findings are unexpected. PiT1 is expressed in a wide variety of organs and cell types and, as a result, the general consensus is that this gene is ubiquitously expressed. However, this short-cut is misleading and although its expression is wide, there are large variations in PiT1 expression levels from an organ to another, or under different physiological conditions [2], [7], [8]. Moreover, cell-type specific expression has not been addressed in most tissues except in bone, which showed that PiT1 is expressed in a subset of hypertrophic chondrocytes and absent from osteoblasts during mouse development [20]. Our results clearly show that the embryo forms, develops and grows without major defects until E11.5 in the absence of PiT1, which demonstrates that PiT1 is dispensable for early development. The over-expression of PiT2 in PiT1-deficient embryos suggests that PiT2 may compensate for the lack of PiT1 up until this stage. However, decreased proliferation and increased apoptosis of PiT1-deficient fetal livers arise despite the over-expression of PiT2 in the liver, demonstrating that PiT2 can not take over the function of PiT1 in the liver, and argues for distinct temporal or tissue-specific roles for PiT1 and PiT2. The novel mouse models described here will be useful tools for future studies addressing this question in more details.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 108 112 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>

###xml 426 429 418 421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 424 429 416 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rb<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 438 442 430 434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Jacks1">[39]</xref>
###xml 444 448 436 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Lee1">[40]</xref>

###xml 640 653 624 629 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;<italic>5/</italic>&#916;<italic>5</italic></sup>

###xml 1744 1748 1712 1716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beg1">[41]</xref>
###xml 1756 1760 1724 1728 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Huser1">[42]</xref>
###xml 1762 1766 1730 1734 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Mikula1">[43]</xref>
###xml 1773 1777 1741 1745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Ganiatsas1">[44]</xref>
###xml 1784 1788 1752 1756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Breitwieser1">[45]</xref>
###xml 1795 1799 1763 1767 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Wada1">[46]</xref>
###xml 1809 1813 1777 1781 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Hilberg1">[47]</xref>
###xml 1858 1862 1826 1830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2316 2320 2284 2288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2399 2403 2367 2371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2439 2440 2407 2408 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2526 2530 2494 2498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 2551 2555 2519 2523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2744 2745 2712 2713 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2768 2771 2736 2739 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 2776 2780 2744 2748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 2812 2816 2780 2784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 2981 2984 2949 2952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck1">[9]</xref>
###xml 2988 2992 2956 2960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 3058 3059 3026 3027 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 3439 3443 3407 3411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1566 1570 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1726 1730 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3449 3453 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Liver formation is a crucial checkpoint in fetal hematopoiesis and development. Livers from E11.5 and E12.5 PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos were very small, contained hematopoietic precursors and disorganized islands of hepatocytes. A small liver can be the result of abnormal hematopoietic cell proliferation, as described in c-myb-deficient embryos [38], or abnormal erythroid cell proliferation and differentiation, as seen in Rb-/- embryos [39], [40]. However, we found normal in vitro proliferative and differentiative function of PiT1Delta5/Delta5 hematopoietic committed progenitor cells making it unlikely that the anemia observed in PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos can be attributed to a hematopoietic cell-autonomous defect. Moreover, although fetal livers are hypoplastic, erythroid progenitors have the ability to migrate there, arguing against a fetal liver homing defect. Liver cells from PiT1Delta5/Delta5 embryos underwent a decrease in proliferation and a massive wave of apoptosis, suggesting that PiT1 provides a proliferation and survival signal for hepatocytes during a defined stage of liver morphogenesis. This result was reinforced by the pattern of expression of PiT1 in the embryo at mid-gestation showing a high and preferential expression in the liver, and the acute re-expression of PiT1 following partial hepatectomy in adult liver, consistent with a crucial role of PiT1 in liver growth. The molecular mechanisms by which PiT1 mediates a pro-proliferative and anti-apoptotic function in the developing liver have yet to be clarified. In PiT1-null mice, the liver bud forms and the following proliferation period needed of expansion of the liver is highly affected. This phenotype is somewhat reminiscent of mice lacking RelA [41], Raf-1 [42], [43], MKK4 [44], ATF2 [45], MKK7 [46] or c-Jun [47]. There is no data in the literature linking PiT1 to signaling pathways and our attempts to detect changes in the phosphorylation of relevant signaling pathways in the liver were unsuccessful (data not shown). As the mammalian target of rapamycin (mTOR) is a kinase that integrates signals from nutrients and growth factors to regulate cell growth and cell cycle progression coordinately, we also investigated the phosphorylation state of S6K1, S6, Akt1 and 4EBP1 proteins but could not show defects in PiT1-deficient MEFs (data not shown). We have shown that the proliferation rate of PiT1-null MEFs is decreased while the Na+-Pi transport activity remains unchanged, most probably due to the over-expression of PiT2 that is observed in PiT1-deficient MEFs. This result is consistent with our recent data identifying a novel function of PiT1, not shared by PiT2, that is related to cell proliferation, and is independent of its Na+-Pi transport activity [9]. In PiT1-null fetal livers we show that PiT2 is overexpressed but that this overexpression does not compensate for the loss of PiT1. Therefore it is tempting to speculate that as in MEFs, HepG2 and HeLa cells [9], a PiT2 overexpression in mutant livers could compensate for a loss of Na+-Pi transport activity (as it is shared by PiT1 and PiT2), but not for a loss of a PiT1-specific function such as the proliferation-related function of PiT1. However, this remains an hypothesis since the generation of new animal models carrying mutations of either function of PiT1 (proliferation- or transport-related) is necessary to determine whether the observed phenotype of PiT1-null mice is due to a loss of either or both function of PiT1.
###end p 85
###begin p 86
###xml 77 78 77 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 569 573 569 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Li1">[19]</xref>
###xml 709 713 709 713 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-VillaBellosta2">[48]</xref>
###xml 830 834 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-VillaBellosta3">[49]</xref>
###xml 1173 1174 1173 1174 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1199 1203 1199 1203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-VillaBellosta2">[48]</xref>
###xml 1205 1209 1205 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Wang2">[50]</xref>
###xml 1320 1324 1320 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1344 1348 1344 1348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Festing1">[51]</xref>
###xml 1391 1395 1391 1395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1625 1629 1625 1629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1878 1882 1878 1882 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Festing1">[51]</xref>
###xml 2306 2313 2306 2313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
To date, most studies conducted on PiT1 have focused on the expression and Na+-Pi transport activity of PiT1 in tissues in which Pi biology plays an important role, mainly bone and vascular physiology. However, recent observations may be related to a transport-independent function of PiT1. Studies conducted in VSMCs have led to the proposal that an increase in Pi influx through the plasma membrane could lead to the to the transdifferentiation of VSMCs in osteoblast-like cells and calcification of the extracellular matrix under high extracellular Pi concentration [19]. Although PiT1 was irrefutably shown to be involved in this process, the mechanisms underlying the action of PiT1 is now being debated [48]. Notably, a recent report shows that under physiological conditions, the Pi-transport activity of PiT1 is saturated [49], implying that only an increase in the capacity (i.e. enhanced expression of functional Pi transporters) can mediate an increase in Pi influx. However, not only such an increase has not been evidenced but the expression of PiT1 in VSMCs is very low, making unlikely that PiT1 mediates its effect on vascular calficification through its Na+-Pi cotransport activity [48], [50]. While we were writing this paper, a technical report describing the generation of null and floxed alleles of PiT1 has been published [51]. The authors have deleted exon 3 and 4 of PiT1 which also led to embryonic lethality at mid-gestation around E12.5, although with a lower penetrance than in our model which may be due to differences in the genetic background used. Similarly to our results, they reported that PiT1-null embryos were anemic, although the origin of the anemia was not investigated and was based only on external observation. Of note, the authors reported possible defects in supercifial vasculature of yolk sac based on visual external observation [51]. However, although we also found that mutant yolk sacs appear white, we used specific endothelial cell immunostaining to show that there were no major vascular defects shortly before the occurrence of embryonic death at E12.5. In summary, although PiT1 does not seem to be essential to the development of a normal vasculature, it remains to be determined whether PiT1 is instrumental to a Pi-induced vascular calcification in vivo through the generation of animals carrying a tissue-specific deletion of PiT1.
###end p 86
###begin p 87
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 144 148 144 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 158 162 158 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 175 176 175 176 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 315 319 312 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Beck2">[10]</xref>
###xml 321 325 318 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer1">[12]</xref>
###xml 327 331 324 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Zoidis1">[13]</xref>
###xml 333 337 330 334 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Suzuki2">[14]</xref>
###xml 339 343 336 340 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Wang1">[16]</xref>
###xml 345 349 342 346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer2">[17]</xref>
###xml 361 365 358 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 375 379 372 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT2</italic>
###xml 429 433 426 430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Nielsen1">[15]</xref>
###xml 482 490 479 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 532 533 529 530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 656 660 653 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 784 788 781 785 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Palmer3">[20]</xref>
###xml 831 835 828 832 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Ravera1">[22]</xref>
###xml 954 958 951 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1040 1044 1037 1041 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0009148-Yoshiko1">[52]</xref>
###xml 1227 1231 1224 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1283 1287 1280 1284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1422 1426 1419 1423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1479 1486 1476 1483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lox/lox</sup>
###xml 1475 1486 1472 1483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>lox/lox</sup></italic>
###xml 1632 1636 1629 1633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 1241 1245 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1288 1292 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1487 1491 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1572 1576 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The regulation of PiT1 has been well documented in bone and cartilage models, due to the requirement of large amounts of Pi in bone physiology. PiT1, but not PiT2, mRNA and Na+-Pi transport were found to be regulated in osteoblast-like and chondrogenic cells by various factors, mainly Pi, IGF-1, BMP2 and TGF-beta [10], [12], [13], [14], [16], [17]. Moreover, PiT1, but not PiT2 is upregulated during osteoblast differentiation [15]. However, all these studies have been conducted in vitro, and it is still not clear whether the Na+-Pi transport function of PiT1 is implicated in these processes in normal physiological conditions. The weak expression of PiT1 in bone, particularly in osteoblasts, its discrete expression in a subset of hypertrophic chondrocytes late in development [20], together with its low transport capacity [22] make it an unlikely candidate to face the tremendous Pi needs for bone and cartilage mineralization. The main role of PiT1 in bone may rather be to mediate extracellular signals, as was recently proposed [52], independently, or additionally, of its transport function. Nevertheless, our data clearly show that there is no developmental defects in both vascular and cartilage compartments of PiT1-depleted mice. Although our results in hypomorphic PiT1 mice show that, at birth, the mineralization of bone was delayed, its rapid normalization argues against a major predominant role for PiT1 in skeleton mineralization. The availability of PiT1lox/lox mice will help at elucidating this particular point using appropriate Cre-expressing mice for generating bone and cartilage-specific deletion of PiT1.
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 43 47 43 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1</italic>
###xml 637 638 637 638 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
In summary, through the establishment of a PiT1 mutant allelic series we have uncovered a specific role of PiT1 in normal liver growth. We have shown that PiT1 is essential to embryonic development, and is non redundant as PiT2 could not compensate for the loss of PiT1. On the other hand, PiT1 seems not to be essential for skeleton and vasculature development. Although this study opens new avenues on the functions of the PiT protein family, the molecular mechanisms leading to the impairment of liver development remain to be elucidated, including open questions of whether the proliferation-associated function of PiT1 and/or the Na+Pi transport activity of PiT1 and PiT2 are involved in the observed phenotypes.
###end p 88

Aberrant splicing of the PiT1neo allele. (A) Schematic representation of the PiT1neo and PiT1Delta 5 alleles, with black boxes representing PiT1 coding sequences. The neo cassette and loxP sites are also depicted. Below the allele are diagrams representing the corresponding mRNAs produced by these alleles, as determined by the RT-PCR analysis shown in B using the primers indicated (arrow heads). (B) RNA isolated from the progeny of PiT1neo/+ or PiT1Delta 5/+ mice was reverse transcribed, and assayed by PCR using the primers indicated. Sequence analysis of these PCR products revealed the aberrant splicing of the PiT1neo allele, as illustrated in the diagram in A. The detection of similar size amplification products in samples derived from wild-type and PiT1neo/neo when primer pair F1R3 was used indicates that some wild-type PiT1 mRNA is produced by the PiT1neo allele.

###xml 449 452 433 436 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 445 452 429 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 461 476 445 452 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup>
###xml 457 476 441 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup></italic>
###xml 622 625 598 601 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 618 625 594 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 634 649 610 617 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup>
###xml 630 649 606 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup></italic>
###xml 859 862 827 830 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 855 862 823 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 871 886 839 846 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup>
###xml 867 886 835 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PiT1<sup>&#916; 5/&#916; 5</sup></italic>
###xml 650 654 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 887 891 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Absence of placental defect in PiT1Delta 5/Delta 5 embryos. (A) External appearance of PiT1+/+ (left) and PiT1Delta 5/Delta 5 (right) placentas at E12.5. (B-C) Haematoxilin and eosin (H&E)-stained placental sections at E12.5. The size and histological appearance of the different layers are comparable between the wild-type and the mutant. Note the presence of less red blood cells in the mutant than in the wild-type. (D-E) Anti-PECAM-1 IHC of PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta 5/Delta 5 placental sections at E12.5 illustrating the presence of endothelial cells in both genotypes. (F-G) Ki67 staining of placental sections from PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta 5/Delta 5 mice. Most cells were positively labelled (white arrow), and few were negative (black arrow), demonstrating active and comparable cycling in both genotypes. (H-I) TUNEL analysis on placental sections from PiT1+/+ and PiT1Delta 5/Delta 5 mice demonstrate a low and comparable level of apoptotic cells (white arrow) in both genotypes. Sections were stained with DAPI to visualize the nuclei (blue). La: labyrinth; St: spongiotrophoblast; Gc: giant cells; Md: maternal decidua. Bars, 1 mm (A), 100 microm (B-I).

Phenotype of PiT1neo/neo mice. (A) Body weight as a function of age. Each point represents mean +/- SD from 3 to 10 measurements. (B) Gross morphological appearance of PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/neo mice at birth. Note the smaller size and paler coloration of the mutant. (C) Gross appearance of PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/neo mice at 15-days of age. (D) Organ weight relative to body weight at 15-days of age. The spleen of the hypomorphic PiT1 mouse is 2.4-fold larger than its wild-type counterpart. ** indicates significant differences as compared to wild-type controls with P<0.01 (Student's t test). (E) Peripheral blood smears from 3-weeks old PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/neo littermates. Numerous red cells with abnormal morphology are present, including echinocytes (black arrows), spherocytes (white arrows), and schizocytes (grey arrows).

Phenotype of PiT1neo/Delta 5 compound heterozygotes. (A) Morphological appearance of PiT1neo/Delta 5 E14.5 embryos (right), as compared to wild-type littermates (left). Note the severe anemia and slight decrease in size. (B-C) H&E staining of E14.5 sagital sections from PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/Delta 5 livers. The mutant liver shows desorganized parenchyme, reduced cellularity and pyknotic nuclei (white arrow). (D-E) H&E staining of E12.5 sections from PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/Delta 5 livers showing no difference between the two genotypes. Bar, 100 microm. (F-G) Close examination of yolk sac membranes from wild-type and PiT1neo/Delta 5 E14.5 embryos demonstrate the presence of a highly developed vasculature (black arrows) characterized by a decrease in red blood cell number. (H-I) May-Grunwald/Giemsa staining of peripheral blood smears from E14.5 PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/Delta 5 littermates. Note the similar morphology of red blood cells, but the higher percentage of nucleated erythrocytes (black arrows). (J) Quantification of the nucleated erythrocytes in the peripheral blood of E15.5 PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/Delta 5 littermates. (K) RT-PCR analysis of the expression of globin chains in E15.5 PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/Delta 5 littermate livers, and expressed as a ratio between fetal and adult expression. * and # indicate significant differences as compared to wild-type controls with P<0.05 and P<0.001, respectively (Student's t test).

Hematologic variables in adult mice, according to genotype. Circulating blood of 3-week-old PiT1+/+, PiT1neo/+ and PiT1neo/neo mice mice was analyzed on a Vet'ABC counter (SCIL, Viernheim, Germany). Reticulocyte count was determined on blood smears using a reticulocyte stain (Sigma). The data shown were obtained from a litter-matched group of mice (n = 3-4) and are representative of three experiments with independent groups of animals. Values are means +/- SD. * and ** indicate significant differences between PiT1neo/neo and wild-type controls with P<0.05 and P<0.01, respectively (Student's t test). There was no significant difference between PiT1+/+ and PiT1neo/+ adults in any assay.

Fatty acid, phospholipids and cholesterol profiles of PiT1+/+, PiT1neo/+ and PiT1neo/neo erythrocyte membranes. a values are given as the mean from three mice in each group +/- SD. The fatty acid contents are expressed as molar percentages. Percentages were significantly different from control by the two-tailed t-test with *P<0.05 and **P<0.01. b Unsaturation expressed as double bond index (calculated as the sum of each unsaturated fatty acid concentration multiplied by its double bond number and divided by the total unsaturated fatty acid concentration). SCD: stearoyl-CoA desaturase index (de novo synthesis of 18:1n-9 from 18:0); MUFA: monounsaturated; PUFA: polyunsaturated; EFA: essential. c values are given as the mean from three mice in each group +/- SD. PE: phosphatidylethanolamine; PI: phosphatidylinositol; PS: phosphatidylserine; PC: phosphatidylcholine; SM: sphingomyelin; acidic: PI+PS; neutral: PE+PC+SM; PE+PS+PI: preferentially internal layer phospholipids; PC+SM: preferentially external layer phospholipids; PL: phospholipids.
